<div id="review_37066292" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/37066292" />
    <a title="LJ" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/250195-lj"><img alt="LJ" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1436467895p2/250195.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/37066292?book_show_action=true">Nov 06, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="LJ" class="user" itemprop="url" name="LJ" href="/user/show/250195-lj">LJ</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/250195-lj?shelf=england">england</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/250195-lj?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/250195-lj?shelf=female_author">female_author</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/250195-lj?shelf=suspense">suspense</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/250195-lj?shelf=middle_ages_5th_cent-1558">middle_ages_5th_cent-1558</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/250195-lj?shelf=historical">historical</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/250195-lj?shelf=novel">novel</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/250195-lj?shelf=1300s">1300s</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer37066292" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7021785057992571432">COMPANY OF LIARS (Hist. Myst-Camelot-England-1348) – VG+<br/>Maitland, Karen – Standalone<br/>Penguin/Michael Joseph, 2008, UK Hardcover – ISBN: 9780718153229<br/><br/>First Sentence: ‘So that’s settled then, we bury her alive in the iron bridle. That’ll keep her tongue still.’<br/><br/>The plague has come to England and nine people have joined together in an attempt to outrun it and find safety. A very disparate group it is: a scarred trader of holy relics, a magician, a musician and his teacher, a storyteller with a deform</span>
  <span id="freeText7021785057992571432" style="display:none">COMPANY OF LIARS (Hist. Myst-Camelot-England-1348) – VG+<br />Maitland, Karen – Standalone<br />Penguin/Michael Joseph, 2008, UK Hardcover – ISBN: 9780718153229<br /><br />First Sentence: ‘So that’s settled then, we bury her alive in the iron bridle. That’ll keep her tongue still.’<br /><br />The plague has come to England and nine people have joined together in an attempt to outrun it and find safety. A very disparate group it is: a scarred trader of holy relics, a magician, a musician and his teacher, a storyteller with a deformity, a pregnant couple, a healer and a white-haired girl who reads runes. As they travel, they share stories, face danger and die--one-by-one. <br /><br />This was a wonderful, unusual, engrossing, compelling book that was so well written, I couldn’t put it down. It has an intriguing cast of characters, about each of whom you learn through the story and through the stories they tell. Each has a secret that is revealed through the story. The narrator, Camelot the relic trader, has a wonderful voice and is the steady core of the group. I did like that the books characters aren’t the titled or wealthy, but neither are they farmers or peasants, but travelers without a constant base. The distinctive roles provide a real richness and tension to the story. The suspense is very well done. With each death the tension rises. But don’t expect this to be your usual murder mystery. It’s a story about secrets and lies, and we’re dealing with the Middle Ages here. <br /><br />The sense of time, place and history created by Maitland is so much a part of the story. This was a brutal, ugly time in which to live with the elements so much a part of daily life. It was also a time of fear, superstition and bigotry. In reading the story, at the culmination of our 2008 Presidential election, I realized that not a lot has changed in almost 700 years, although our living conditions are much better and one certainly wouldn’t wanted to live back then. The history is well researched and well presented, including a map, historical notes and a glossary. The suspense is very well done all the way to the last sentence. With each death the tension rises. But don’t expect this to be your usual murder mystery. It’s a story about secrets and lies, and we’re dealing with the Middle Ages here. <br /><br />Had it not had a prologue which set the mood but had not direct relationship to the story and had it not included portents, which I despise, I would have given it an “Excellent” rating. Don’t be put off by the size of the book. It was an absolutely great read and I’m off to find out what else Ms. Maitland has written.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="7021785057992571432" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_49607931" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/49607931" />
    <a title="Ann" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/153-ann"><img alt="Ann" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1216931198p2/153.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/49607931?book_show_action=true">Mar 17, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ann" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ann" href="/user/show/153-ann">Ann</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer49607931" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5646628119632888559">I have so many wishes. I wish I’d paid less attention to the “stunning reinterpretation of the Canterbury Tales!” part of the book jacket and noticed that all the blurbs were from people who <i>write scary books</i>. If you are like me – for whatever reason, I have read <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/568236.A_Distant_Mirror_The_Calamitous_14th_Century' title='A Distant Mirror The Calamitous 14th Century by Barbara W. Tuchman' rel='nofollow noopener'>A Distant Mirror</a> yet cannot sit through even the most banal mystery book without crapping my pants – then this is not for you. I wish I had the foresight to realize that even though I was rolling my eyes with every other page, I would g</span>
  <span id="freeText5646628119632888559" style="display:none">I have so many wishes. I wish I’d paid less attention to the “stunning reinterpretation of the Canterbury Tales!” part of the book jacket and noticed that all the blurbs were from people who <i>write scary books</i>. If you are like me – for whatever reason, I have read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/568236.A_Distant_Mirror_The_Calamitous_14th_Century" title="A Distant Mirror The Calamitous 14th Century by Barbara W. Tuchman" rel="nofollow noopener">A Distant Mirror</a> yet cannot sit through even the most banal mystery book without crapping my pants – then this is not for you. I wish I had the foresight to realize that even though I was rolling my eyes with every other page, I would get completely engrossed in the (terrifying) last few chapters and barely escape before the pants-crapping could begin. But most of all I wish that Ms Maitland – who obviously put a lot of effort into researching this book and knows her 1348 – had ditched the (oddly, incompletely selective) glossary and spent more time on the actual prose. Why, why, why, as someone writing in 2008, would you make your beloved characters spout chestnuts like “when the lamb lies with the ewe, it is like mother coupling with child” when they are barely developed enough to serve your many, ponderous, and drudgingly reiterated themes (hint: liars!), but not enough to make them behave as actual humans who might have once lived? I guess what I’m saying is, I wish it was more like the Canterbury Tales.</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_105056573" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780141031910" href="/book/show/5263376-company-of-liars">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/272909-blair?shelf=first-novels">first-novels</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/272909-blair?shelf=historical">historical</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/272909-blair?shelf=mystery-thriller-etc">mystery-thriller-etc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/272909-blair?shelf=2000s-release">2000s-release</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer105056573" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6086247744888072497">The second book I've read by this author in as many months, this was just as enjoyable and satisfying as <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/5263374.The_Owl_Killers' title='The Owl Killers by Karen Maitland' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Owl Killers</a>. Maitland is brilliant at bringing the sights, sounds and smells of the 14th century to life, and the cast of characters was fantastic; I imagine it must be very hard to make each member of such a large group distinctive, but every one of the band of travellers was almost immediately memorable. My only problem with the lengthy narrative was that some parts were too similar to </span>
  <span id="freeText6086247744888072497" style="display:none">The second book I've read by this author in as many months, this was just as enjoyable and satisfying as <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/5263374.The_Owl_Killers" title="The Owl Killers by Karen Maitland" rel="nofollow noopener">The Owl Killers</a>. Maitland is brilliant at bringing the sights, sounds and smells of the 14th century to life, and the cast of characters was fantastic; I imagine it must be very hard to make each member of such a large group distinctive, but every one of the band of travellers was almost immediately memorable. My only problem with the lengthy narrative was that some parts were too similar to others, and this was occasionally confusing; for example, some of the murders that took place appeared, later in the story, to have been 'solved' seemingly without there being any actual confirmation of who the killer was, although it could be that I somehow missed these details in amongst all the other action. The author certainly seems to have found her niche writing stories set in late-medieval England, and if there are more I will definitely read them. I would recommend Maitland's books to anyone who loves historical fiction, and indeed anyone who's interested in getting into it, as they're so accessible and fun to read.</span>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer18087572890783511172">I enjoyed this quite a bit.<br/><br/>It is definitely a very slow burn. It starts slow with some foreshadowing and follows the company's travel in great detail, so it isn't a book for people who are looking for a quick read with a lot of action.<br/><br/>However I was quite pleasantly surprised with the detail put into each character, and there are a number of twists and turns that I didn't see coming which made the slow pace well worth it. The author has also put work into creating the atmosphere and sticking as c</span>
  <span id="freeText18087572890783511172" style="display:none">I enjoyed this quite a bit.<br /><br />It is definitely a very slow burn. It starts slow with some foreshadowing and follows the company's travel in great detail, so it isn't a book for people who are looking for a quick read with a lot of action.<br /><br />However I was quite pleasantly surprised with the detail put into each character, and there are a number of twists and turns that I didn't see coming which made the slow pace well worth it. The author has also put work into creating the atmosphere and sticking as close as she can to the time period and I felt she did a wonderful job with that. It is marked as Fantasy however, and does have some fantastical elements, but those don't detract from the story.<br /><br />This is my first book by this author so I'm excited to see what else she has out there.</span>

<div id="review_1969997140" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1969997140" />
    <a title="Debbie " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/23953835-debbie"><img alt="Debbie " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1600782368p2/23953835.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1969997140?book_show_action=true">Apr 16, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Debbie " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Debbie " href="/user/show/23953835-debbie">Debbie </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780385341691" href="/book/show/3184477-company-of-liars">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1969997140" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14251889845099736037">3.5 stars. Very well-written and absorbing tale. The characters and events held my attention for the most part. My only criticism is that I felt the author could've gotten to the point/ending a little quicker--I know the characters are on a slow journey through countryside, but at times it felt like the novel's pace was matching the horse's when it was pulling the wagon through muddy terrain. Fortunately, that wasn't often and the overall story was very good. </span>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer4090301986473475897">Plague has arrived in the north of England. A group of nine find solace together traveling through these hostile times. Winner is harsh, villagers unwelcoming and suspicion behind to fester within the group.<br/><br/>I enjoyed this a lot, well until the last few pages where two events arrived out of nowhere and threw me totally! Were there clues? Not sure how I feel about that part.</span>

<div id="review_34623671" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/34623671" />
    <a title="Carrie Kitzmiller" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/65745-carrie-kitzmiller"><img alt="Carrie Kitzmiller" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1538244210p2/65745.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/34623671?book_show_action=true">Oct 05, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Carrie Kitzmiller" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Carrie Kitzmiller" href="/user/show/65745-carrie-kitzmiller">Carrie Kitzmiller</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/65745-carrie-kitzmiller?shelf=2008">2008</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer34623671" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4454372382407328373">Company of Liars by Karen Maitland is a reinterpretation of Chaucer’s Canterbury Tales. Set in 14th century England, during a time of fear, religious power, and superstition, it is the story of nine travelers trying to escape the Plague. As they travel inland, it becomes apparent that each one carries a secret. One by one, the secrets are exposed, with deadly consequences.<br/><br/>There is Zophiel, the traveling magician whose wagon full of boxes is a constant source of worry. No one knows what is in the</span>
  <span id="freeText4454372382407328373" style="display:none">Company of Liars by Karen Maitland is a reinterpretation of Chaucer’s Canterbury Tales. Set in 14th century England, during a time of fear, religious power, and superstition, it is the story of nine travelers trying to escape the Plague. As they travel inland, it becomes apparent that each one carries a secret. One by one, the secrets are exposed, with deadly consequences.<br /><br />There is Zophiel, the traveling magician whose wagon full of boxes is a constant source of worry. No one knows what is in them, but there seems to be someone following them who does.<br /><br />Osmond and Adela, a young couple expecting their first child, also travel with the group. They seem to be of too high a class to be traveling with the wanderers.<br /><br />Rodrigo and Jofre are musicians from Italy. Jofre has a hot head and a taste for wine, as he drinks to get away from his own secrets.<br /><br />Pleasance is a midwife who hides her true identity, while helping to keep the travelers healthy and caring for Adela in her pregnancy.<br /><br />Narigorm is a white-haired child who enchants everyone who meets her - but there is a darkness in her.<br /><br />The story is narrated by Camelot, a traveling peddler who sells saints’ relics and artifacts. We see and experience the story through Camelot’s eyes and ony at the end do we realize that his secret is the biggest of all.<br /><br />Karen Maitland is an amazing writer who digs into the faults and weaknesses of human nature, the things that people prefer to keep hidden. She uses the child Narigorm as a catalyst for the characters to confront their true natures, for better or for worst. The results are disturbing, mystical, and all too believable.<br /><br />Even though I wasn’t completely crazy about this book, I kept reading because of the quality of Maitland’s writing, and because I wanted to see how it would end. She does an excellent job of slowly revealing the truths about the nine travelers, piece by piece. The religion and superstition that permeate the book create an eery atmosphere that becomes terrifying as the book progresses - culminating in an ending that made me shiver. Though the ending was clever in that way, I still didn’t care for the twist. But that’s just me - and I would still recommend this to any lovers of historical fiction.<br /><br />3 out of 5 stars<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="4454372382407328373" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('rVN54brrn2ujKQK+FFpu0LyC29Yip+T+WgWEsEENA8neknneC9D3rqeiFDLjc95oQ0ji+j+M/CFDub3lbAwa8g==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('aeTSr+b37azGMSWjYWcV8QgmWQwbM3xsle506oetQ50aJdKQV8yFacK6My+WTqVJ9+xgIAYYZLOMUk2/qqxapg==')})
  }
//]]>

The relic is said to be cursed: anyone who touches it will meet an untimely and gruesome end. Several decades later, the Cross turns up in the possession of a dealer, robbed and murdered en route to Glastonbury. Investigating the death, Bernard Knight\'s protagonist, Crowner John learns of its dark history. In Oxford in 1269, the discovery of a decapitated monk leads Ian Morson\'s academic sleuth William Falconer to uncover a link to the relic. In 1323, in Exeter, Michael Jecks\' Sir Baldwin has reason to suspect its involvement in at least five violent deaths. Thirty years later, several suspicious deaths occur in Cambridge - and, once again, the tainted relic has a crucial part to play. Parris\'s gripping novel, Bruno\'s pursuit of this rare knowledge brings him to London, where he is unexpectedly recruited by Queen Elizabeth I and is sent undercover to Oxford University on the pretext of a royal visitation. Included are chapters on the history of piracy, stretching back to ancient Greece and Rome; essentials of language and dress; notable pirate role models, including Blackbeard and Captain Kidd; what to expect of life at sea; the best weapons to have; how to capture a prize on the high seas and much more.\n\n\nAuthor Stephen Turnbull has studied the archives and traveled to pirate locations around the world in researching this fictionalized account, written as a pirate’s training manual for a young recruit based in the year 1793—a golden age for piracy. Illustrated throughout with artifacts, documents, and prints of the time as well as modern reconstructions, this lively and engaging manual provides answers to all the questions readers may have wondered about—did they really walk the plank, keep parrots, or bury treasure and mark it with an X on the map? Pirate: The Buccaneer’s (Unofficial) Manual answers these questions and more, covering with authority every aspect of what it was really like to be a pirate.<\/span>\n  <a       <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/335919.Karen_Maitland">About Karen Maitland</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/335919.Karen_Maitland"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1286434516p3/335919.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/335919.Karen_Maitland">Karen Maitland
</a></div>

followers

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer8308372444588520342"><br/>Karen Maitland has recently moved to the wonderful county of Devon and has a doctorate in psycholinguists. She is fascinated by the myth and magic of the Middle Ages, which she draws on for her novels. She experienced the medieval lifestyle for real, when she worked for eighteen months in a rural village in Nigeria, living without electricity, plumbing or sanitation. <br/><br/>Her first medieval thriller wa</span>
  <span id="freeText8308372444588520342" style="display:none"><br />Karen Maitland has recently moved to the wonderful county of Devon and has a doctorate in psycholinguists. She is fascinated by the myth and magic of the Middle Ages, which she draws on for her novels. She experienced the medieval lifestyle for real, when she worked for eighteen months in a rural village in Nigeria, living without electricity, plumbing or sanitation. <br /><br />Her first medieval thriller was 'Company of Liars', was set at the time of the Black Death in 1348. This was followed by 'The Owl Killers', about the beguinages, the medieval cities of women. 'The Gallows Curse' is set in the reign of bad King John and 'Falcons of Fire and Ice', which is a dark thriller, set in Portugal during the Inquisition and Iceland at the time of the Reformation. She is published by Michael Joseph/Penguin.<br /><br />Karen is also one of six historical crime writers known as the Medieval Murderers – Philip Gooden, Susannah Gregory, Michael Jecks, Bernard Knight and Ian Morson – who together write an annual joint murder-mystery novel, including 'The Sacred Stone', 'Hill of Bones' and 'The First Murder' published by Simon &amp; Schuster.<br />	<br /><br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="8308372444588520342" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
